009                                               A BSTRACT
010
011            Within the framework of federated learning, we introduce two novel strategies:
012            New Lazy Aggregation (NLA) and Accelerated Aggregation (AA). The NLA strat-
013            egy reduces communication and computational costs through adaptive gradient
014            skipping, while the AA strategy accelerates computation and decreases communi-
015            cation costs via adaptive gradient accumulation. Building upon these innovative
016            strategies and compression techniques, we propose two new algorithms: FedBN-
017            LACA and FedBACA, aimed at minimizing bidirectional communication costs.
018
               We provide theoretical guarantees for client participation (either full or partial) in
               these algorithms under non-convex settings and heterogeneous data. In the context
019
               of non-convex optimization with full client participation, our proposed FedBN-
020
               LACA and FedBACA algorithms achieve the same convergence rate of O 1/T
021            as their non-tight counterparts. Extensive experimental results demonstrate that
022            our protocols facilitate effective training in non-convex environments and exhibit
023            robustness across a wide range of devices, partial participation, and imbalanced
024            data.
025
026
027   1   I NTRODUCTION
028
029   Federated Learning (FL) is a promising machine learning (ML) framework that enables collaborative
030   model training without sharing data. This approach ensures that data privacy is protected, as data
031   does not need to leave the ownerвҖҷs possession McMahan et al. (2017). FL models involve edge clients
032   or devices, such as smartphones and personal computers (PCs), training local ML models using
033
      their own data without sharing. Instead of sending raw data to a central server (e.g. cloud server),
      the edge client updates the parameters of the local server model (e.g. smartphone, PC updates).
034
      The server then generates a shared global ML model by aggregating local parameter updates. In
035
      FL, traditional distributed stochastic gradient descent (SGD) is unsuitable for challenging federated
036   learning scenarios, where data does not follow independent homogeneous distributions and only
037   a small fraction of clients participate in each communication round. To address this issue, many
038   federated optimization methods use local client updates. To reduce significantly the amount of
039   communication required to train the model, local clients update their models multiple times before
040   communicating with the server. One of the most popular FL methods is the FedAvg algorithm
041   proposed by McMahan et al. (2017), in which the global model is updated by averaging over multiple
042   local SGD update steps.
043   Although FedAvg algorithm can be trained without sharing data and achieve good results, it in
044   practice still presents challenges in FL. 1) Lack of adaptivity. As SGD-based updates may not be
045   suitable for stochastic gradient noise with heavy-tailed distributions, which usually occur when
046   training large models Devlin et al. (2019); Brown et al. (2020); 2) Unaffordable communication.
047   Repeated synchronization of the uplink and downlink between the client and the server leads to
048   significant communication overhead, but some of these parameters are passed non-essential. Here, the
049   uplink represents a transmission from clients to servers and the downlink represents a transmission
050
      from server to clients.
051   Many works have researched the aforementioned issues. 1) For adaptivity in the federated learning
052   framework, Reddi et al. (2020) proposed the FedAdam algorithm and its variants Tong et al. (2020);
053   Wang et al. (2022a); Wu et al. (2023), which integrate the adaptive gradient approach. 2) Recently,
      to reduce communication costs, three approaches have been developed: (i) Local approach Huang


                                                         1
      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


054
      et al. (2023); Li & Wang (2019); Li et al. (2019b); Mishchenko et al. (2022); Karimireddy et al.
055   (2019a). The local devices implement multiple rounds of optimization before sending the information
056   to the server. This reduces the rounds of global communication, thereby having an overall lower
057   communication cost. (ii) Compression methods Reisizadeh et al. (2020); Chen et al. (2021); RichtaМҒrik
058   et al. (2023); Beznosikov et al. (2023). During each round of communication, the local devices send
059   compressed information to the server, reducing communication costs through some compression
060   mechanisms. (iii) Lazy aggregation algorithmChen et al. (2018b); Sun et al. (2019); Ghadikolaei et al.
061   (2021); Mishchenko et al. (2022). Some parameters may be similar to those of the previous round, so
062   they do not need to be transmitted (i.e., the parameters of the previous round are used in the current
063
      round), which also effectively reduces the communication cost.
064   However, although the lazy aggregation algorithm provides a strategy to reduce communication costs,
065   it is more difficult to implement in practice, especially in joint learning where only some clients
066   are involved in the training. Although these algorithms have achieved great success in reducing
067   communication costs, they are unidirectional in the sense that they are uplink communication, not
068   downlink communication. A natural thought is: How do we design a simple and more efficient
069
      strategy to improve communication efficiency based on bidirectional communication? In this
      paper, we initially introduce two innovative updated strategies, namely NLA and AA. These strategies
070
      are subsequently applied to the FedAMS and FedCAMS algorithms as outlined in Wang et al.
071
      (2022a). Furthermore, we advance the development of bidirectional communication-efficient adaptive
072   algorithms within a non-convex framework and in the context of heterogeneous data.
073
074   Main contributions
075   вҖў We present two novel communication strategies for joint learning in federated learning (FL),
076   referred to as NLA and AA, which improve upon the existing LAG algorithmChen et al. (2018b);
077   Sun et al. (2019); Mishchenko et al. (2022). In contrast to conventional approaches, NLA and AA
078   do not require parameters from multiple iterations; rather, they utilize only the parameters from the
079   preceding iteration along with those from the current iteration. This characteristic enhances their
080   adaptability and simplifies their implementation.
081   вҖў We propose two novel and efficient adaptive optimization techniques for communication:
082   FedNLACA and FedACA . Both methods enhance communication efficiency and adaptability within
083   the context of joint learning. The FedNLACA algorithm notably decreases communication costs by
084   employing real error feedback, a compression strategy, and our proposed NLA strategy, all while
085   preserving high accuracy. Similarly, the FedACA algorithm effectively reduces communication
086   costs and sustains high accuracy through the use of real error feedback, a compression strategy,
087
      and our proposed AA strategy.  It is important to highlight that FedNLACA and FedACA attains a
      convergence rate of O 1/T .
088
089   вҖў We have developed a novel cross-device compatible adaptive joint optimization method, referred to
090   as FedBNLACA and FedBACA, which employs two strategic approaches to facilitate a reduction in
091   bidirectional communication costs for both uplink and downlink transmissions. A convergence analy-
092   sis was performed under conditions of general non-convexity and data heterogeneity,  demonstrating
093
      that both FedBNLACA and FedBACA can also attain a convergence rate of O 1/T .
094   вҖў Extensive experiments on various benchmarks showed that our proposed algorithms are well
095   adaptive in training real-world machine learning models.
096
097
098   2   R ELATED WORK
099
100   Adaptive Gradient Methods: Adaptive gradients (Zeiler, 2012; Duchi et al., 2011; Kingma &
101   Ba, 2014; Reddi et al., 2018) are a series of algorithms that effectively reduce the relatively slow
102   convergence and over-sensitivity to parameters of gradient descent methods in the face of heavy-tailed
103   stochastic gradients, and are heavily used to train large networks.
104   Federated Learning: FedAvg was introduced by McMahan et al. (2017) as the inaugural algorithm
105   for federated learning (FL). By employing periodic model averaging, this approach significantly
106   mitigates communication overheads. Initial studies focused on the analysis of FL algorithms within a
107   homogeneous data framework, while more recent investigations have expanded the scope of federated
      learning to encompass heterogeneous data environments (non-iid) and non-convex models (Li &


                                                        2
      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


108
      Wang, 2019; Li et al., 2019a; Sahu et al., 2018; Yang et al., 2019; Wang et al., 2022a)). (Li et al.,
109   2019a; Sahu et al., 2018) proposed FedProx and FedDANE algorithms for federated optimization
110   against heterogeneity. Wang et al. (2022a)gave theoretical results of data heterogeneous federated
111   learning under the conditions of adaptive methods. In this paper, we follow the ideas of Wang et al.
112   (2022a). Numerous studies have been conducted that build upon the FedAvg framework, including
113   notable contributions such as FedNova Wang et al. (2020), and SCAFFOLD Karimireddy et al.
114   (2019a), as well as various other adaptations of FedAvg (Yang et al., 2021b; Wang et al., 2022a).
115   In a recent advancement, Reddi et al. (2020) introduced several adaptive federated optimization
116   techniques, including FedAdagrad, FedYogi, and FedAdam, aimed at addressing the convergence
117
      challenges associated with FedAvg. Additionally, Chen et al. (2020) presented Local AMSGrad,
      while Tong et al. (2020) introduced a suite of federated adaptive gradient methods that incorporate
118
      calibration mechanisms.
119
120   Effective methods of communication: Many methods to reduce communication costs have been
121   proposed in federated learning, three main ideas are 1) multiple rounds of local iteration methods
122   (Elgabli et al., 2022; McMahan et al., 2017; Li et al., 2019a; Sahu et al., 2018), 2) compression and
123
      error feedback (Reisizadeh et al., 2020; Elgabli et al., 2022; Haddadpour et al., 2020; Wang et al.,
      2022a), 3) lazy aggregation (Sun et al., 2020; Mao et al., 2022; Chen et al., 2018b; Sun et al., 2019).
124
      Most of the above methods are only unidirectional (uplink), and although (Sun et al., 2020; Wang
125
      et al., 2022b) considered bidirectional algorithms, they did not consider the heterogeneity problem in
126   FL, the involvement of some of the servers in the training as well as the related theoretical guarantee,
127   and the adaptive problem. Moreover, their strategies to reduce the communication cost are difficult to
128   implement under heterogeneous partial clients participation. Therefore, how to give simple strategies
129   to reduce communication cost, and how to design adaptively efficient algorithms for bidirectional
130   communication with partial clients participation is the focus of this paper.
131                                       вҲҡ
      Notation: For vectors x, y вҲҲ Rd , x, x2 , x/y denote the n element-wise square root, square, and
132   division of the vectors. For vector x and matrix A, k В· k denotes the `2 norm of vector/matrix, i.e.,
133   kxk = kxk2 and kAk = kAk2 . In algorithms, t denotes the t-th iteration. The m is the number of all
134   clients/devices.

      Remark 3.1. The NLA Strategy presented herein represents a modification of the lazy aggregation
217   method as described in previous works Chen et al. (2018b); Sun et al. (2019). This approach is
218   characterized by its operational simplicity, necessitating only a comparison with the parameters from
219   the preceding iteration. As an innovative lazy aggregation technique, the NLA Strategy effectively
220   diminishes communication costs by minimizing the number of communication parameters required.
221   (The NLA strategy assesses whether the difference between the parameters from the (t вҲ’ 1)th and
222   t-th iterations falls within a minimal threshold, indicating that these parameters are closely aligned.
223   If this proximity is confirmed, the parameter from the (t вҲ’ 1)th iteration is retained in place of the
224   parameter from the t-th iteration.)

239
240   Remark 3.2. The AA strategy is a novel acceleration method designed to reduce communication
241
      costs by speeding up the process. The proposal of this strategy is based on a fundamental motivation:
      when the parameters of the (t вҲ’ 1)th iteration are very close to the parameters of the tth iteration, it is
242
      possible to achieve an update of both steps at once (i.e., by adding the parameters of the (t вҲ’ 1)th
243
      and tth iterations). This core idea is consistent with the principles of the NLA algorithm. Through
244   adaptive accelerated iterative descent, the AA strategy can effectively reduce communication costs. It
245   is worth noting that even without the AA strategy, the iterative process of conventional algorithms
246   can still achieve results similar to those of the AA strategy, but a more in-depth analysis of the AA
247   strategy will be reserved for future research.

252   4.1   F EDERATED N EW L AZY AGGREGATION AMSG RAD AND F EDERATED ACCELERATION
253         AMSG RAD

      In this section, we present two new frameworks of the adaptive algorithm: Federated New Lazy
255
      Aggregation AMSGrad (FedNLAA) and Federated Accelerated AMSGrad (FedAA). In FedNLAA
256   and FedAA algorithms. Оёt is the t-th iteration t of the global model parameters. At iteration t, the
257   participating client i in the selected subset St (of size n) receives the model Оёt from the server, i.e.,
258    i
      Оёt,0 = Оёt . Then, the client performs K steps of local SGD updating with local learning rate О·l to
259   get the local model Оёt,Ki

372   Remark 4.4. Note that Corollary 4.2 suggests that Theorems 4.3 and 4.4 directly relate to the global
373   variance Пғq2 . Such convergence rate is consistent with the partial participation result of FedAvg in the
374   non-i.i.d case in Yang et al. (2021a). It is shown that the global variance has more influence on the
375   convergence behavior in partial participation cases. This is especially true for highly non-i.i.d cases
376   where Пғg is large. The effect of the number of local updates, K, is complex. In partial participation
377   settings, the larger value of K results in a slower convergence, while full participation suggests the
      opposite. A similar slowdown was also seen in Wang et al. (2022a).

      4.3        F ED BNLACA AND F ED BACA A LGORITHMS
413
414   Algorithm 3 gives only a one-way algorithm to reduce the cost of communication (unplink). In the sec-
415   tion, we propose two bidirectional communication algorithms (uplink and downlink) with efficiently
416   adaptive non-convex optimization: Federated Bidirectional New Lazy Aggregation Compression
417   AMSGrad (FedBNLACA) and Federated Bidirectional Accelerated Compression AMSGrad (Fed-
418   BACA). The detailed procedure is given in Algorithm 2.
419   Next, we show the convergence analysis for FedBNLACA and FedBACA. Due to the space limit, we
420   only show the full participation setting and leave the partial participation setting in Appendix E.2.

      5    E XPERIMENTS
468
      We compare our proposed algorithms with several state-of-the-art algorithms (FedAvgMcMahan et al.
469
      (2017), FedAMS, FedCAMS(Wang et al. (2022a)), Fedadam (Reddi et al. (2020)). We use MNIST
470
      and Fashion-MNIST datasets, and models by MLP and CNN, respectively. A total of 100 clients
471   for all federated training experiments are used. Set the partial participation rate to 0.5, i.e. in each
472   round, the server selects 50 clients out of 100 to participate in communication and model updating. In
473   each round, the client completes 3 local epochs with batch size 32. In experiments, we respectively
474   sample Independent Identical Distribution (I.I.D.) and non-I.I.D. client data from the dataset. Choose
475   compression rate in Topk to be 1/8 and 1/128. For parameters C and D, the values are not too large.
476   From theoretical analysis, the larger the values of C and D, the larger the errors. In addition, C and
477   D are too small, and basically does not help вҲҡto reduce communication cost. We also verify this result.
478   We suggest that C and D in the vicinity of Оұmlg m .
479
      Figures 1-2 represent the relationship between the accuracy of prediction and communication Bits
480   when the model is CNN and the I.I.D. client data is sampled from Fashion-MNIST dataset. From
481   Figure 1, we can find that (i) the proposed algorithm FedNLAA not only communicates fewer
482   Bits than the other three state-of-the-art algorithms, but also has higher accuracy; (ii) our proposed
483   algorithms (FedNLACA and FedBNLACA) require only few communication Bits to achieve good
484   accuracy, especially the bidirectional compression algorithm FedBNLACA requires even fewer Bits.
485   These shows that our proposed algorithms are communication efficient. From Figure 2, we can find
      that (i) the proposed algorithm FedAA algorithm can converge more quickly than the other three

      algorithms, thus disguising the reduction of communication cost; (ii) FedACA and FedBACA can
518   also converge quickly and with higher accuracy than the other three algorithms, especially FedBACA.
519
520   Figures 3-4 represent the relationship between the accuracy of prediction and communication Bits
521
      when the model is CNN and the non-I.I.D. client data is sampled from Fashion-MNIST dataset..From
      Figure 3, we can find that (i) the proposed algorithm FedNLAA not only communicates fewer Bits
522
      than the other three state-of-the-art algorithms, but also has higher accuracy; (ii) FedAvg performs the
523
      worst; (iii) our proposed algorithms (FedNLACA and FedBNLACA) require only few communication
524   Bits to achieve good accuracy, especially the bidirectional compression algorithm FedBNLACA
525   requires even fewer Bits. These also show that our proposed algorithms are communication efficient.
526   From Figure 4, we can find that (i) the proposed FedAA algorithm can converge more quickly than
527   the other three algorithms, thus disguising the reduction of communication cost; (ii) our algorithms
528   (FedACA and FedBACA) can also converge quickly and with higher accuracy than the other three
529   algorithms, especially FedBACA.
530
531
532   6    C ONCLUSION
533
534   We propose two novel strategies: NLA and AA in the framework of federated learning. They are
535   simple to operate and effective in reducing the communication cost. The NLA strategy achieves
536   communication cost reduction by reducing the amount of information passed and AA strategy reduces
537   the communication cost by accelerating computation. By combining our proposed strategies with
538   compression techniques, we design FedNLAA and FedAA algorithms, which not only achieve com-
539   munication cost reduction in one-way, but also extend them to bidirectional algorithms (FedBNLACA
      and FedBACA), which achieve communication cost reduction in bidirectional as well.

      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025

703                                            Appendix
704
705   A     F ED NLACA AND F EDACA A LGORITHMS
706
707   A.1    P ROCEDURE OF F ED NLACA AND F EDACA
708
709   In order to reduce communication costs, we propose Federated New Lazy Aggregation Compression
710   AMSGrad (FedNLACA) and Federated Accelerated Compression AMSGrad (FedACA). These two
711
      algorithms combine two of our proposed strategies(strategy 1 (FedNLACA), strategy 2 (FedACA) )
      and compression techniques. The detailed procedure is given in Algorithm 3.
712
713

741   Theorem A.2. The upper bound for mintвҲҲ[T ] E[kвҲҮf (Оёt )k2 ] contains three terms: The first two terms
742
      decrease as T increases, and this term tends to zero as t tends to infinity. The last term relates to the
      local stochastic variance Пғl and global variance Пғg . In the i.i.d setting, where the global variance is
743
      zero and each worker has the same data distribution, i.e., Пғg = 0, the variance term в„Ұ will be smaller.

             вҲҡ

751   Remark A.2. Corollary A.1 suggests that with sufficient large T , FedCAMS achieves the desired
752
      O( вҲҡT1Km ) convergence rate which matches the result for its uncompressed counterpart FedNLAA

      and FedAA. In addition, when T = O(Km), mintвҲҲ[T ] E kвҲҮf (Оёt )k = O T1 . This suggests that
                                                                        2

      much on the accuracy.

      Remark A.3. When the parameters C = D, Оұn       = 1, the result of Theorem A.3 becomes the result of
811
      Theorem A.4. The upper bound for mintвҲҲ[T ] E[kвҲҮf (Оёt )k2 ] contains three terms: The first two terms
812
      decrease as T increases, and this term tends to zero as t tends to infinity. The last term relates to the
813   local stochastic variance Пғl and global variance Пғg . In the i.i.d setting, where the global variance is
814   zero and each worker has the same data distribution, i.e., Пғg = 0, the variance term в„Ұ will be smaller.
815
      Corollary A.2. Suppose we choose local learning rate О·l = Оҳ( вҲҡT1 K ) and the global learning
816                вҲҡ
817   rate О· = Оҳ( Kn) , the convergence rate for FedNLACA,FedACA in Algorithm 1 under partial
818   participation scheme without replacement sampling is
819                                                         вҲҡ
                                                     2
                                                              K
820                                  min E kвҲҮf (Оёt )k = O вҲҡ      .
821
                                     tвҲҲ[T ]                   Tn
822   Remark A.4. Note that Corollary A.2 suggests that Theorem A.3,A.4 directly relates to the global
823   variance Пғq2 . Such convergence rate is consistent with the partial participation result of FedAvg in the
824   non i.i.d case in Yang et al. (2021a). It is shown that the global variance has more influence on the
825   convergence behaviour in partial participation cases. This is especially true for highly non i.i.d. cases
826
      where Пғg is large.The effect of the number of local updates, K, is complex. In partial participation
      settings, larger values of K result in slower convergence, while full participation suggests the opposite.
827
      A similar slowdown was also seen in Wang et al. (2022a).
